# Dashboard PRD Plan: Forge Surfaces

**Source:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md`
**Generated:** 2026-04-25
**Source hash:** `e536e24c29af14ade4086f7b87d3835f483f8cce3894c3bb82af9cb327d6aa3e`
**Section tasks:** 66
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/plans.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/prds.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/research.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/events.rs`

### DASH-13-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:7` through `24`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`, `knowledge-learning`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

The Forge section is where users do the substantive creative work of specifying what agents should do, composing multi-step plans, running research workflows, observing execution, and replaying past episodes to learn from them.

Where Fleet is about *which agents exist and what they are*, Forge is about *what they do and how that work is composed*.

Forge contains five pages: PRDs, Plans, Research, Execution, Replay.

- **PRDs** — a pipeline for refining ideas into published specifications.
- **Plans** — structured specifications for agent work: DAGs of tasks, dependencies, checkpoints.
- **Research** — multi-agent research workflows where several agents collaborate on a topic.
- **Execution** — the live view of running plans: what's in progress, what's blocked, what's completed.
- **Replay** — step through past episodes for debugging and learning.

Forge is used by Solo Operators running specific tasks, Fleet Orchestrators composing workflows across many agents, Arena Competitors iterating on configurations, and Meta-Builders orchestrating recursive generation flows.

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `152`
- Section hash: `c572e9eb36ef710a90fad7406a9c9895e3e5670f5fdc24c3ce7b352500eb83c7`

- The Forge section is where users do the substantive creative work of specifying what agents should do, composing multi-step plans, running research workflows, observing execution, and replaying past episodes to learn from them.
- - **PRDs** — a pipeline for refining ideas into published specifications. - **Plans** — structured specifications for agent work: DAGs of tasks, dependencies, checkpoints. - **Research** — multi-agent research workflows where several agents collaborate on a topic. - **Execution** — the live view of running plans: what's in progress, what's blocked, what's completed. - **Replay** — step through past episodes for debugging and learning.

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "PRDs," block height, lens switcher.

**Section 04 — PRD Pipeline.** (Note: the current dashboard numbers this "04" per its section ordering; retain the numbering.) Description: "From raw idea to published specification. Agents draft, research-enhance, and consolidate PRDs autonomously."

**Pipeline Status row**: three hero KPI cards at top showing the three pipeline stages:
- **Ideas** (count).
- **Drafts** (count).
- **Published** (count).

Beneath the three cards, a summary line: "N PRDs in pipeline" and a "Consolidate PRDs" action (invokes a meta-operation where an agent synthesizes multiple PRDs into a coherent superset).

A fuller status row below with:
- Total PRDs, Ideas, Drafts, Published — as compact stat tiles.
- "Stale" count (PRDs that haven't moved in a while).
- "Has Plan" count (PRDs with an associated plan).

**Section — Idea Capture.** Content:

A text input: "Describe a product idea..." with a "Capture Idea" button.

Chips above the input suggesting recent notable ideas or templates (e.g., "Decentralized model routing mesh," "Cross-venue funding rate arbitrage engine," "HDC-based anomaly detection for DeFi").

The capture flow: user types an idea, clicks capture, an agent converts the idea into an Idea card in the Kanban below. The agent may enhance the idea with research (via the user's configured Research Scout or similar agent) — this is optional and configurable.

**Section — PRD Kanban.** Description: "Capture ideas to start the pipeline."

Content: a three-column Kanban board:
- **Idea** column (count).
- **Draft** column (count).
- **Published** column (count).

Each column shows a list of cards. Each card:
- Title.
- Identifier (slug).
- Stage tag (IDEA / DRAFT / PUBLISHED).
- Primary action: "Draft" button on Idea cards, "Generate Plan" button on Published cards, additional actions via context menu.
- Secondary info: age, author, short summary.

Users can drag cards between columns (manual stage transitions). Most transitions happen through agent-assisted actions (click "Draft" to have an agent refine the idea into a structured draft).

**Section — Recent Activity.** Content: a feed of recent PRD events — ideas captured, drafts refined, PRDs published, plans generated. Useful for seeing pipeline momentum.
````

### DASH-13-S015 -- Purpose

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:127` through `132`
**Heading level:** H3

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Purpose

Plans are structured specifications of work: DAGs of tasks with dependencies, checkpoints, expected outcomes. A plan is "here's what will happen, in order, conditionally." Plans are authored, shared, executed, and replayed.

In the current dashboard, Plans is a thin page. This specification expands it into a full authoring-and-management surface.
````

- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-13-S018 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:143` through `170`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Plans," block height, lens switcher. Primary action: "New Plan" (opens Plan Composer — see `19-authoring-surfaces.md`).

**Section 01 — Plan Library.** Description: "Structured specifications for agent work. DAGs of tasks, dependencies, and checkpoints."

Content: a grid of plan cards. Each card:
- Plan name.
- Short description.
- Status (Draft, Ready, Running, Completed, Failed, Archived).
- Agents associated (count and portraits).
- Gate configuration summary.
- Estimated duration / cost.
- Ownership badge.

Cards sortable by recent, name, status. Filterable by domain, status, owner.

**Section 02 — Active Plans.** Content: a condensed Plans row for plans currently Running. Each with:
- Plan name.
- Progress indicator (step N of M).
- Current step summary.
- Time elapsed / estimated remaining.
- Quick actions: Pause, Abort, View in Execution.

**Section 03 — Plan Templates.** Description: "Reusable plan definitions. Fork and customize."

Content: a grid of plan template cards. Similar to Agent Templates but for plans. Built-in plan templates (debugging workflow, research workflow, arena submission workflow) plus user-published ones.
````

### DASH-13-S019 -- Plan authoring (linked from this page via "New Plan")

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:171` through `184`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Plan authoring (linked from this page via "New Plan")

Plan authoring deserves dedicated treatment in `19-authoring-surfaces.md`. Briefly, plan authoring supports:

- Visual DAG editor: nodes are tasks, edges are dependencies.
- Task types: run-agent, run-gate, branch-on-outcome, wait-for-event, human-checkpoint, publish-output, fork-plan.
- Variables passed between tasks.
- Conditional branches based on task outcomes.
- Checkpoints where the plan pauses for human review.
- Loops with termination conditions.
- Sub-plan invocation (a task that runs another plan).

A plan is a first-class object with its own URL, its own execution history, and its own composability.
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `91`
- Section hash: `4d72963faa00d1cae31d50e8afca7cbc1ac94db3a1568be5ff8b3a4dd92e3122`

### DASH-13-S030 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:237` through `272`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Research," block height, lens switcher. Primary action: "New Research" (starts a new research session).

**Section 01 — Active Research.** Description: "Research sessions currently running. Multi-agent investigations in progress."

Content: cards for currently-running research sessions. Each card:
- Topic / question.
- Agents involved (portraits).
- Phase indicator (Gathering, Analyzing, Synthesizing, Producing).
- Progress bar.
- Time elapsed.
- Partial findings preview (if any).

Live updates as research progresses.

**Section 02 — Recent Research.** Description: "Completed sessions, with findings."

Content: cards for recently-completed research sessions. Each card:
- Topic.
- Date completed.
- Agents involved.
- Summary of findings (short).
- Link to full output.
- Publication status.

**Section 03 — Research Templates.** Content: plan-style templates but specifically for research workflows. Examples:
- "Deep topic dive" (one topic, one agent, thorough source gathering).
- "Multi-source synthesis" (gather N sources, synthesize across them).
- "Comparative analysis" (compare multiple options).
- "Adversarial review" (one agent researches, another critiques).

Users can pick a template when starting new research.

**Section 04 — My Research Archive.** Content: the user's archived research sessions, searchable by topic, date, agents involved, tags.
````

### DASH-13-S042 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:337` through `366`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Execution," block height, lens switcher.

**Section 01 — Executing Plans.** Description: "Plans currently running. Each plan, each step, each decision."

Content: an expandable list of currently-executing plans. Each item expands to show:

- **Plan header**: plan name, owner, duration elapsed, estimated remaining.
- **DAG visualization**: the plan's DAG rendered, with nodes colored by status (complete, in-progress, blocked, failed, upcoming). Users can see at a glance where the plan is.
- **Current step panel**: the active step's detail, with live output.
- **Event feed**: scoped event stream showing events from this plan's execution.
- **Controls**: Pause Plan, Abort Plan, Skip Step (with confirmation), Replay Last Step.

The list can show many plans; each collapsed entry shows enough to know status without expansion.

**Section 02 — Blocked or Waiting.** Description: "Plans paused for human review, waiting for external signals, or blocked."

Content: a list of plans that need attention. Each shows:
- Plan name.
- Reason for block (waiting for human, waiting for gate, dependency failed).
- Time blocked.
- Primary action (Resume, Review, Re-route).

Users can quickly process the backlog of blocked plans.

**Section 03 — Recent Completions.** Description: "Plans that just finished."

Content: a feed of recently-completed plans (last 24 hours by default, adjustable), each showing outcome, duration, key outputs, agents involved.
````

- Section hash: `e8ae4029351aa41f1f549a82e977239f179796cf24106222f81f6e5d51b81172`

### DASH-13-S050 -- Purpose

````markdown
### Purpose

Step through past episodes — the unit of learning in Roko. An episode captures everything that happened during one end-to-end task execution: the initial state, the context assembled, the LLM requests and responses, the tool calls, the gate verdicts, the outcome. Replay is where users learn from past executions.
````

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Replay," block height, lens switcher.

**Section 01 — Episode Selector.** Content:

A search and filter bar:
- Search by episode ID, task keyword.
- Filter by agent, domain, outcome, time range.
- Sort by recent, cost, duration, outcome.

A list of episodes matching filters. Each row:
- Episode ID and timestamp.
- Agent portrait and name.
- Task summary.
- Outcome tag (success / failure / partial).
- Duration and cost.

**Section 02 — Episode Detail (when one is selected).** Description: "Every tick, every decision, every tool call. Step through what happened."

The section becomes the dominant content when an episode is selected.

**Metadata row**: episode ID (mono), agent, start time, end time, duration, outcome, cost, tier mix (T0/T1/T2 percentages).

**Timeline scrubber**: a horizontal timeline of the episode's events. Users can scrub to any point to see state at that moment. Clickable events become selectable.

**Main view** (split into panels):

- **Left — Event list**: every event in the episode, selectable. Clicking an event focuses the rest of the view on that moment.
- **Center — Snapshot**: what was happening at the selected event. Context assembled, LLM request (if applicable), LLM response, tool call, gate verdict.
- **Right — Annotations**: user-added notes on this episode. Comments can be added to specific events.

**Playback controls**: step forward, step back, play at variable speed, pause, jump to start/end.
````

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click an episode → select it for detail view.
- Scrub timeline → jump to any moment.
- Playback controls.
- Annotate: add comments tied to specific events. Comments persist and are visible to all users with access to the episode.
- Fork episode: create a new plan that starts from this episode's final state (useful for "try different approach from here").
- Share episode: copy a URL that opens this episode's Replay view.
````

````markdown
### Deferred

- Differential replay: compare two episodes side by side. Later.
````

- - Counterfactual replay: "what if we had used a different context?" — expensive but powerful. Later.
- - Collaborative replay: multiple users scrubbing the same episode in real time. Later.
- - Export episode as a training example. Later.

**Tables extracted:**
- None extracted from this section.

- None extracted from this section.

### DASH-13-S061 -- The spine of creation-to-execution

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/13-forge-surfaces.md:497` through `502`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`, `knowledge-learning`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### The spine of creation-to-execution

Forge is the spine that runs ideas → specifications → plans → execution → episodes → learning. A user can follow a single piece of work all the way through: capture an idea in PRDs, refine to a draft, publish, generate a plan from the PRD, run the plan in Execution, replay episodes from the execution to understand what happened.

This spine is a navigation path. Users should feel the flow — each page has clear "next step" affordances forward and "back to source" affordances back.
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section hash: `6e4510b93373a73f505a46051d85d3521826b4183c2322c193ad0c0f11265563`

````markdown
### Meta integration

Meta-Builders who create meta-agents that produce new agents will often work in Forge — a meta-agent's output is typically plans, which run in Execution, which produce episodes visible in Replay. The Forge section is agnostic to whether the plan's creator is a human or a meta-agent.
````
